IV. 
WORLD 
BANK 
GROUP 
STRATEGY 
A. 
Consistency 
of 
the 
PRSC 
with 
the 
Country 
Assistance 
Strategy 
(CAS) 
5 
1. 
The 
proposed 
PRSCl 
is 
premised 
on 
the strong 
record 
Tanzania 
has 
maintained 
during 
the 
past 
five 
years 
in 
successfully 
implementing 
macroeconomic and structural 
reforms 
supported 
by 
the Bank, 
the 
IMF, 
and other 
donors. Successive 
Poverty Reduction 
and 
Growth 
Facility 
(PRGF) 
reviews, 
PERs, 
and supervision missions 
for 
the 
PSAC 
have 
confirmed 
these 
achievements. 
52. 
The 
high 
case 
scenario 
of 
the 
CAS 
for 
fiscal 
2001-03 
envisaged a 
Public 
Expenditure 
Reform 
Credit 
(now 
PRSC) 
to 
support 
Tanzania’s 
efforts 
in 
combating 
poverty, 
spur 
rural 
development,  and 
promote protection 
of 
the 
environment 
as 
a basis 
for 
sustainable 
development. 
It 
was 
planned 
that  the  PRSC 
would 
be 
the 
instrument 
through 
which 
the 
Bank 
would 
systematically 
address 
the 
issues 
of 
poverty 
reduction 
across 
sectors 
that 
were 
identified 
in 
the 
PRS. 
The 
triggers 
for 
moving 
to 
this 
scenario 
were specified 
in 
the 
Tanzania 
fiscal 
2001-03 
CAS 
and 
all 
actions 
under 
the 
triggers 
have 
been 
implemented. 
Aside 
from 
maintaining 
a  stable 
macroeconomic 
environment, 
the 
triggers 
included 
an 
increased 
poverty 
focus 
of 
public 
expenditures; 
the  development 
of 
coherent 
sector 
programs 
for 
health, 
education,  water, 
environment,  and 
agriculture combined 
with 
strengthened 
capacities 
for 
the 
implementation 
of 
these 
sector programs; 
and 
a 
variety 
of 
governance 
measures 
to 
fight 
corruption 
and strengthen 
public 
sector 
financial 
management. 
The 
fulfillment 
of 
these 
triggers 
is 
assessed 
in 
annex 
8. 
53. 
A 
new 
CAS 
for 
the 
period 
fiscal 
2004-06 
is 
currently 
under 
preparation 
and 
will 
be 
presented 
to 
the 
Board 
together 
with 
the 
next 
year’s 
PRS  progress 
report. 
To 
support 
the 
implementation 
of 
Tanzania’s 
PRS, 
efforts 
to 
maintain 
macroeconomic 
stability 
will 
continue, 
but 
the 
focus 
is 
increasingly 
shifting 
to 
sector-level 
and 
cross-cutting 
public 
sector management 
issues. 
The 
key 
challenge 
is 
to 
replicate 
the 
excellent macroeconomic 
policy 
and 
implementation 
record 
at 
the 
sector 
level 
to 
facilitate 
economic transformation and 
poverty 
eradication. 
54. 
One 
of 
the 
key 
themes 
of 
the 
new 
CAS 
will 
be 
the 
full 
alignment 
of 
Bank 
instruments 
with 
the 
principles 
of 
local 
ownership 
and leadership 
of 
development 
efforts 
set 
out 
in 
the 
PRS 
and, 
more specifically, 
in 
the 
TAS. 
Because 
government 
policies 
and the government 
budget 
are 
the 
key 
instruments 
in 
implementing 
the 
PRS, 
the 
Bank 
will 
increasingly 
provide 
general 
budget 
support, a 
shift 
that 
has 
already been 
initiated 
under 
the 
current 
CAS. 
Over 
the 
medium 
term, 
the 
PRSC 
will 
become 
the 
main 
instrument 
for 
the 
transfer 
of 
financial 
resources  and 
policy 
dialogue. 
A 
shift 
in 
lending 
modalities 
is 
considered 
necessary, 
because sector 
interventions 
through 
investment projects have been 
characterized 
by 
variable 
local 
ownership 
and 
have 
not 
always 
been 
well 
integrated 
with 
other 
sectoral activities,  and 
thus 
sustainability 
has 
been 
low. 
Also, 
development 
of 
government 
systems 
has 
received 
limited 
support, 
because 
most 
donors 
have tended 
to 
focus 
on 
their 
own 
aid 
delivery 
mechanisms. 
The 
shift 
to 
programmatic 
lending 
was 
precipitated 
by 
the 
government’s 
call for 
a 
change 
in 
donors’ 
lending modalities. The 
shift 
in 
Tanzania 
was 
justified 
on 
three 
grounds: 
(1) 
the 
PRS 
has 
evolved 
into 
the 
overarching framework 
for 
policy 
dialogue 
and 
formulation both 
within 
Tanzania and 
between 
government and the 
donor 
community, 
(2) 
progress 
on 
the 
macroeconomic 
front 
has 
lessened 
the 
need 
for 
traditional 
adjustment  lending, 
and 
(3) 
progress 
in 
planning 
and 
budget 
management 
provides 
confidence 
that 
public 
resource 
allocations 
are 
consistent 
with 
PRS 
priorities. 
55. 
It 
is 
envisaged 
that 
the 
transition 
will 
be 
a gradual one. 
Initial 
PRSC 
support 
will 
coexist 
with 
budget 
and 
investment 
support 
to 
well-articulated 
sector 
programs 
and 
technical 
assistance 
to 
the 
development 
of 
government 
systems 
and capacities necessary 
for 
the 
increased 
reliance 
on 
18 
Page  29
government 
systems 
in 
the 
provision 
of 
external 
support 
and the 
switch 
to 
program 
support. 
This 
approach, 
in 
which 
the 
PRSC 
initially 
covers 
primarily 
cross-cutting 
issues 
and 
policy 
dialogue 
and 
only 
gradually 
embraces 
sectoral 
support, 
provides 
scope 
for 
learning 
on 
both 
the 
Bank 
and 
the 
government 
sides 
and a 
continued evaluation 
of 
the 
appropriateness 
of 
this 
approach. 
56. 
Although 
integrating 
sectoral support 
into 
the 
PRSP 
would 
reduce 
transaction 
costs and 
strengthen 
the 
leverage 
of 
central 
ministries 
to 
achieve 
alignment 
of 
sector programs 
with 
the 
PRS 
priorities, 
there 
are also 
several 
potential 
risks. 
These 
include 
the 
risk 
that the 
coordination 
requirements  inherent 
in 
a 
multisectoral 
operation 
might 
overstretch 
human 
resources 
and 
institutional 
capacities, 
the 
increased 
risk 
to 
budget 
predictability 
if 
a 
significant 
amount 
of 
resources 
is 
provided 
through 
a 
single 
instrument, 
and 
the 
potential 
for 
a 
loss 
of 
donor cohesion 
and 
partnership 
if 
possibilities 
for 
participation 
in 
well-defined 
joint 
sector  approaches 
are 
reduced. 
Further 
work 
to 
clarify 
these 
issues 
will 
be 
undertaken 
in 
preparation 
of 
the 
CAS. 
In 
line 
with 
the proposed 
graduated approach 
to 
the 
integration 
of 
sector 
issues 
in 
the 
PRSC. 
A 
decision 
on 
the 
subsequent 
integration 
of 
other 
sectors 
in 
the 
PRSC 
will 
be 
made based 
on 
the 
experience 
gained 
in 
Tanzania 
as 
well 
as 
other 
countries. 
57. 
The 
proposed 
PRSCl 
is 
a 
blend 
of 
a 
credit 
and an 
IDA 
grant. 
The fiscal 
2001-03 
Tanzania 
CAS 
provided 
for 
HIPC 
debt 
relief 
to 
enable 
the 
country 
to 
increase spending 
for 
poverty-focused 
programs. 
The 
government 
intends 
to 
use 
the 
IDA 
grant  component 
to 
protect 
or 
increase 
allocation 
of 
resources 
to 
sectors 
with 
the 
largest 
impact 
on 
poverty 
and 
human 
development. 
Within 
each 
sector, 
poverty 
priorities 
are 
being 
specified 
in 
the 
context 
of 
the 
Tanzania 
PRS 
and 
its 
annual 
updates. 
Domestic 
support 
for 
reforms 
is 
particularly 
important 
at 
this 
stage 
to 
cushion 
against a 
potential 
backlash 
from 
privatization 
of 
the 
large 
utilities 
and 
infrastructure 
and 
ensure 
continuance 
of 
the 
focus 
on 
supporting 
poverty 
reduction  beyond 
the 
tenure 
of 
the  current 
reformist 
president. 
IDA 
grants 
will 
therefore 
enable and sustain a 
virtuous 
cycle 
of 
reforms. 
B. 
Supporting 
PRS 
Implementation 
through 
a 
PRSC 
58. 
The 
primary aim 
of 
the 
PRSC 
is 
to 
facilitate 
the 
implementation 
of 
the 
PRS 
through 
budget 
support and 
monitor 
whether 
adequate 
progress 
is 
being 
made 
toward 
the 
objectives 
defined 
in 
the 
PRSC, 
including 
progress 
toward 
the 
MDGs. 
Particular 
emphasis 
is 
put 
on 
the 
establishment 
of 
an 
adequate 
monitoring 
framework 
in 
line 
with 
the 
poverty 
monitoring 
master 
plan. 
Disbursements made according 
to 
the 
PRSC 
framework 
will 
be 
contingent 
on 
progress 
toward 
the 
PRS 
objectives 
in 
the 
medium 
term. The 
objective 
of 
the 
PRSC’s 
monitoring 
function, 
using 
the 
PRS 
monitoring 
framework, 
is 
to 
provide 
the authorities 
with 
financial 
resources and leverage 
to 
coordinate 
sector 
development programs 
with 
the 
PRS. 
In 
those 
areas 
where 
the 
PRSC 
focuses 
on 
outcome 
monitoring, 
the 
policy 
dialogue  generally 
takes 
place 
in 
the 
context 
of 
sector 
development 
programs, 
particularly 
in 
health 
and 
education. 
59. 
Aside 
from 
monitoring 
overall 
PRS 
objectives, 
the 
PRSC 
is 
also  a 
vehicle 
for 
policy 
dialogue 
on 
selected 
areas 
of 
the 
PRS 
agenda. 
Figure 
3 
shows 
areas 
of 
the 
PRS 
where 
the 
PRSC 
will 
mainly 
focus 
on 
the 
monitoring 
of 
outcomes and those 
areas 
where 
the 
PRSC 
will 
provide 
the 
framework 
for policy 
dialogue 
and 
the 
implementation 
of 
specific 
actions. 
60. 
With 
respect 
to 
most 
of 
the 
components 
of 
Tanzania’s 
strategy 
to 
enhance 
human 
capabilities, 
survival, 
and 
well-being-including 
health, 
education, 
social 
well-being, 
vulnerability, and 
environment-the 
PRSC 
will 
mainly 
focus 
on 
the 
establishment 
of 
appropriate 
monitoring 
systems 
and the 
actual 
monitoring 
of 
progress 
toward 
the 
PRS 
objectives. 
Financial 
support and 
technical 
assistance 
in 
these 
areas 
is 
provided through 
a 
series 
of 
sectoral programs, 
including 
sector 
development 
programs 
for 
health 
and education,  supported 
by 
the 
Bank 
and 
other 
donors. 
PRSCl 
and 
PRSC2 
will 
focus 
on 
progress 
in 
institutionalizing 
the 
monitoring 
and 
19 
Page  30
evaluation 
systems, 
and  PRSC3 
will 
include 
an 
assessment 
of 
whether 
implementation 
of 
Tanzania’s 
poverty 
reduction 
strategy 
is 
having 
the 
expected 
impact 
on 
outcomes. 
61. 
The 
policy 
dialogue 
on 
PSD 
and governance, 
which 
was the 
focus 
of 
the 
PSAC, 
will 
be 
continued 
under 
the 
PRSC. 
In 
addition, the PRSC 
will 
also 
serve 
as 
a 
vehicle 
for 
policy 
dialogue 
on 
sustaining macroeconomic stability, 
rural 
development, 
export 
growth,  and 
the 
environment. 
The 
PRSC 
will 
leverage 
the 
Bank’s 
policy 
dialogue,  and other 
Bank 
and 
donor 
instruments 
will 
be 
used 
to 
provide 
technical 
assistance 
to 
define 
and 
implement 
reforms, 
including 
support 
to 
the 
public 
sector 
reform 
program 
(PSRP), 
the 
Parastatal 
Reform 
Commission, 
the 
local 
government 
reform 
program, and 
the 
legal 
sector 
reform 
program. 
Efforts to 
reduce 
income 
poverty 
are 
also 
supported 
through 
infrastructure  projects 
in 
the 
transport 
and 
energy 
sectors 
and support 
to 
the 
ASDP. 
Figure

PRS 
Implementation through a 
PRSC

62. 
To 
summarize, 
the 
PRSC 
will 
support 
government 
efforts 
to 
reduce 
poverty 
at 
three levels. 
Firstly, 
it 
supports 
measures 
spelt 
out 
in 
the 
PAF 
policy matrix 
that 
are 
expected 
to 
contribute 
directly 
to 
the 
reduction 
of 
income 
poverty. 
This 
includes 
reforms 
in 
the 
areas 
of 
agricultural 
and 
rural 
development 
which 
are 
intended 
to 
raise 
agricultural 
productivity 
and 
thus 
enhance 
the 
incomes 
of 
the 
population 
in 
rural 
areas, 
were 
poverty 
is 
most 
widespread  and 
most 
deeply 
entrenched. 
Private 
sector 
development 
and 
strengthening 
of 
the 
business 
environment, 
and 
legal 
and 
administrative 
reform 
to 
enhance 
the 
functioning 
of 
land,  credit, 
and 
labor 
markets 
are 
intended 
to 
foster 
economic 
growth 
and 
enhance 
employment opportunities, 
as 
access 
to 
formal 
and 
informal 
sector 
employment 
has 
been 
identified 
in 
the 
PRS 
as 
one 
of 
the 
key 
areas 
for 
sustainable 
poverty 
reduction. 
63. 
The 
second 
area 
of 
impact 
is 
through 
monitoring 
and 
leveraging 
progress 
in 
the 
implementation 
of 
sectoral programs 
to 
reduce 
poverty, 
covering 
the 
priority 
sectors 
identified 
in 
20 
Page  31
the 
PRS, 
i.e., 
primary 
education,  basic  health, 
water, 
rural 
roads, 
agricultural 
research 
and 
extension, 
the 
judiciary, 
and 
HIV/AIDS. 
The 
PRSC 
policy 
dialogue 
focuses 
on 
the 
establishment 
of 
a 
robust 
monitoring 
and 
evaluation 
system 
that 
allows 
an 
assessment 
of 
the 
impact and 
results 
of 
sectoral 
programs.  The 
information 
derived 
from 
the 
monitoring 
and evaluation 
system 
will 
then  feed 
into 
the 
assessment 
of 
progress 
towards 
the PRS objective, 
on which 
future 
PRSC 
support 
will 
be 
contingent. 
Finally, 
the 
resources 
provided 
through the 
PRSC 
complement 
government and other donor 
resources 
in 
financing 
priority 
programs 
for 
poverty 
reduction. 
The 
well 
developed 
participatory 
PER-MTEF 
process 
provides 
a 
mechanism 
for 
the 
monitoring 
of 
the 
use 
of 
resources. 
64. 
Finally, 
at the 
third 
level 
are 
cross-sectoral actions 
to 
strengthen 
public 
sector 
performance 
and 
enhance 
the 
efficiency 
and 
effectiveness 
in 
the 
use 
of 
resources.  These 
measures 
will 
have 
a 
direct impact 
on 
poverty 
reduction 
as 
they 
enhance 
public 
sector 
capacity 
to 
implement 
poverty 
reduction 
programs 
in 
the 
priority 
sectors 
and 
generate 
additional 
funds 
for 
poverty 
reduction 
by 
reducing 
leakages 
in 
the 
form 
of 
low 
allocative 
or 
operational 
efficiency 
of 
public 
expenditures. 
Key 
areas 
of 
reform 
include 
strengthening 
of 
financial 
management 
through 
the 
implementation 
of 
the 
public 
financial 
management 
reform 
program, 
strengthening 
of 
the 
national audit office, 
implementation 
of 
pay 
reform 
coupled 
with 
improved 
performance 
management 
in 
the 
public 
sector, 
procurement  reform,  the 
implementation 
of 
anti-corruption 
strategies,  and  enhanced 
efficiency 
in 
the 
use 
of 
development 
assistance. 
C. 
PRS 
Alignment 
between the 
Bank 
and 
Other 
Donor 
Programs 
in 
Support 
of 
the 
Common Goals 
for  Coordination 
of 
Support 
65. 
Consultations 
with 
the 
government 
and  donors 
emphasized 
four 
main 
goals 
and 
mechanisms 
for 
coordinating 
policy 
dialogue, 
taking 
into 
account 
the 
government’s 
desire 
for 
greater coherence and 
efficiency 
in 
supporting 
poverty reduction 
initiatives 
in 
Tanzania. 
The 
clear 
poverty 
focus 
of 
all 
operations 
is 
guided 
by 
the 
homegrown 
PRS and 
its 
rolling 
updates 
as 
the 
framework 
for 
determining 
priorities 
and 
assessing 
the 
impact 
of 
chosen 
interventions. 
Coherence 
in 
policy 
dialogue  around 
the 
PRS 
and 
the 
progress 
review 
process 
applies 
not 
only 
to 
cross-cutting 
issues 
but 
also 
to 
the 
sector-wide 
approaches. 
Efficiency 
in 
the 
approaches 
to 
policy 
dialogue 
and 
performance 
assessment 
is 
essential 
to 
the 
delivery 
of 
support 
for 
poverty 
reduction. 
Given 
the 
high 
transactions 
cost 
of 
multiple 
policy 
dialogues  and 
forms 
of 
support 
to 
poverty 
reduction, 
a 
common goal 
is 
to 
rationalize 
and 
ensure 
consistency 
of 
dialogue 
and 
performance 
assessment. 
There 
is 
a 
strong 
plea 
by 
all 
parties 
involved 
for 
a 
unified 
performance 
assessment 
process, 
with 
room 
for 
individual 
judgment. 
Enhanced 
flexibility 
and 
predictability 
of 
resource 
flows 
is 
achieved 
by 
adopting 
a 
medium-term framework 
and 
offering 
support 
through 
the 
budget 
(exchequer).

Integrative 
Processes 
66. 
Through 
a 
now 
open 
PER-MTEF 
process, 
Tanzania 
has 
adopted 
an 
ongoing, 
participatory, 
and 
strategic 
expenditure 
allocation framework 
and mechanisms 
for 
reviewing 
the 
integrity 
and 
effectiveness 
of 
the 
budget. 
Donors 
have 
progressively 
moved toward 
greater 
coordination 
and 
flexibility 
in 
supporting 
public 
spending 
programs 
through 
sector-wide 
approaches and 
budget 
21 
Page  32
support.  The 
Multilateral 
Debt 
Fund 
and 
now 
the 
PRES 
are 
important 
donor 
coordination 
initiatives 
that 
have 
helped 
to 
emphasize 
the 
poverty 
focus 
of 
public 
spending 
and 
develop 
an 
agreed 
framework 
for 
monitoring 
progress 
in 
strategic 
allocation 
of 
spending 
in 
favor 
of

public 
services. 
The 
PRS 
consolidated 
these 
initiatives 
and 
in 
turn 
benefited 
from 
the 
participatory 
approaches 
and 
partnerships. 
67. 
donor-government 
dialogue 
and 
technical 
assistance: 
Six 
key, 
cross-cutting integrative 
processes, 
inter 
alia, 
form 
the 
basis 
for 
coordinated 
1. 
The 
PRS 
approved 
in 
August 
2000 
provides 
the 
framework 
for 
result-oriented 
poverty reduction interventions 
by 
the 
government, 
its 
external 
partners, 
and 
the 
private 
sector. 
Priority 
sector 
programs 
are 
integrated 
into 
this 
framework through 
planned 
actions 
to 
meet 
the 
PRS 
targets, 
and 
a 
common 
poverty monitoring 
system 
has 
been 
adopted. 
PRS 
progress 
reports 
serve 
both 
monitoring 
and 
updating 
purposes. 
2. 
The 
TAS 
has 
been adopted 
as 
the 
framework 
for 
improving 
the 
overall impact 
of 
development 
assistance 
on 
Tanzania’s 
development. 
3. 
The 
country-led 
annual 
PERs 
provide 
participatory 
open 
review 
of 
the 
effectiveness 
and 
integrity 
of 
public 
spending 
as 
well 
as 
public 
expenditure 
management. 
The 
MTEF, 
developed under 
a participatory  PER 
process, 
is 
the 
main 
strategic resource 
allocation 
mechanism. 
4. 
The 
PSRP 
focuses 
on 
providing 
coordinated 
support 
for improving public 
service 
delivery. 
5. 
The 
national framework 
for 
good 
governance 
supports 
anticorruption 
programs, 
enhancement 
of 
democratic  practices, 
devolution 
of 
authority  to 
lower-level 
government 
and 
communities, 
and 
legal 
reforms 
to underpin positive 
changes 
in 
the 
conduct 
of 
business. 
6. 
Annual 
Consultative 
Group 
meetings 
have been 
held 
in 
Tanzania 
for 
the 
past 
three 
years 
and 
have 
focused 
on 
the 
joint 
review 
of 
PRS 
implementation. 
7. 
There 
are 
ongoing efforts 
for 
further 
harmonization 
of 
these 
processes 
to 
reduce 
duplication 
and 
ensure 
consistency 
of 
advice.

with Other

Related

68. 
The  Bank’s

for

has

aligned 
with 
the

of 
the  PRS. 
Support 
for 
basic 
education 
is 
being 
provided 
through a 
three-year 
Sectoral 
Adjustment 
Loan 
(SECAL), 
which 
became 
effective 
in 
January 
2002. 
In 
its 
first 
year 
after 
being put 
into 
effect, 
it 
is 
running 
concurrently 
with 
the 
PSAC 
and 
will 
run 
thereafter 
with 
PRSCl 
and PRSC2. 
Support 
for 
the 
health 
sector 
is 
provided through 
an 
8- 
year 
adaptable 
programmatic loan 
(APL), 
which 
will 
run 
concurrently 
with 
the 
proposed 
PRSCl 
. 
Coordination 
between 
the 
two 
is 
enabled 
by 
the 
PRS 
process. 
There 
is 
also 
an 
11-year 
APL 
to 
support 
public 
service 
reforms 
in 
collaboration 
with 
donors. 
A 
prospective 
accountability 
and 
governance 
operation 
(ATIP) 
is 
under 
preparation 
and 
will 
provide 
technical 
support 
for 
strengthening legal, 
procurement, 
audit, 
and 
watchdog 
systems. 
Although 
not directly 
integrated 
into 
the 
support 
envisaged under 
the 
PRSC, 
these 
and 
other 
individual 
projects 
and 
programs 
in 
the 
Bank’s 
portfolio 
dovetail 
with 
Tanzania’s 
overall 
PRS. 
Specific  projects 
to 
support 
the 
implementation 
of 
the 
PRS 
include 
rural 
water, 
rural 
roads, 
and 
local 
government 
support 
projects, 
all 
of 
which 
are 
presently 
under 
preparation.

Alignment 
with the 
PRBS 
69. 
The 
government 
has 
reached agreement 
with 
11 
donors6, 
accounting 
for 
more than 
60 
percent 
of 
total official 
development 
assistance 
to 
Tanzania, 
to 
establish 
the 
PRBS 
facility 
to 
support 
the 
implementation 
of 
the  PRS. 
Using 
this 
facility, 
the 
donors  have 
agreed 
to 
seek 
improved 
flexibility, 
reporting, and 
predictability 
of 
flows 
through 
the 
budget. 
To 
ensure 
impact, 
the 
government 
and donors 
have 
agreed 
on 
a 
rolling,  annually reviewed 
and updated 
PAF 
for 
monitoring 
progress 
in 
implementing 
agreed 
reforms 
under 
the 
PRBS. 
These 
reforms 
target 
improved 
effectiveness 
of 
public 
services, 
a better 
incentive 
environment, 
minimized 
resource 
leakage, 
and 
strengthened 
accountability. 
To 
unify 
policy 
dialogue 
and 
minimize 
costs 
associated 
with 
multiple 
dialogues, 
the 
PRBS  donors  and 
the 
government 
have 
decided 
to 
use 
existing 
processes 
for 
policy 
dialogue. 
70. 
The 
PRSC 
program, 
aligned 
with

the

serves 
as 
the 
joint 
framework 
within 
which 
prior 
actions 
for 
each 
PRSC 
are developed and 
assessed. 
Consistency 
of

in

and performance 
assessment 
will 
be

through 
a 
common

process 
and 
harmonized 
policy 
dialogue. 
Both

and 
the 
PRBS 
are 
single- 
or 
two-tranche 
operations 
with

of

based

actions 
or

72. 
A 
PAF 
has 
been 
fully 
discussed 
with 
individual 
ministries, 
departments, 
and 
agencies 
(MDAs) 
for priority 
and

As

such

which would 
undermine 
efficiency 
objectives 
and

Gradual

is 
envisaged and 
analytic 
work 
toward 
this 
goal 
has 
been 
planned.

Harmonization 
and 
Alignment 
of 
Processes 
74. 
The 
government 
budget 
process 
provides 
the 
key 
anchor 
for 
the 
PRSC 
and 
PRBS 
and 
most 
other 
integrative 
processes. 
Because 
one 
of 
the 
objectives 
is 
to 
enhance 
the 
predictability 
of 
donor 
assistance, 
the 
processes are sequenced 
with 
the 
objective 
of 
providing 
a 
firm 
commitment 
to 
the 
availability 
of 
budget 
support 
in 
the 
next 
fiscal 
year 
before 
the 
government’s 
budget 
speech 
in 
June. 
Negotiation 
of 
PRSCs 
will 
thus 
typically 
take 
place 
in 
March 
to 
allow 
government 
to 
factor 
PRSC support 
into 
the budget 
preparation. 
Similarly 
for 
the 
PRBS 
donors, 
the 
annual 
review 
takes 
place 
at 
the 
same 
time, 
although 
not 
all 
donors are able 
to 
make 
firm 
commitments 
for 
the 
full 
year at 
that 
time 
and 
some 
donors 
release 
their 
budget 
support 
in 
two 
or 
more 
tranches. 
The 
annual PRS 
progress 
report 
and 
its 
joint 
staff 
assessment 
will 
typically 
be 
issued 
concurrently 
with 
or 
shortly before 
the 
PRBS 
annual 
review 
and PRSC 
negotiations.

Results 
Orientation 
of 
Tanzania 
PRSC 
Operations 
75. 
The 
results 
orientation 
of 
the PRSC covers 
two 
levels. Foremost, 
the 
PRSC supports 
the 
implementation 
of 
the 
PRS. Broad-based 
progress 
toward 
achieving 
the PRS objectives 
is 
the 
key 
results 
area 
against 
which 
the 
effectiveness 
of 
PRSC  support 
should 
be 
judged. 
This 
area 
of 
results 
orientation 
is 
reflected 
in 
the 
PRSC 
through 
the 
strong focus 
on 
establishing 
a 
robust 
M&E 
system 
for 
the 
PRSC 
and

development 
of 
indicators that 
allow 
continuous 
tracking 
of 
progress 
in 
the 
pursuit 
of 
the 
PRS targets. 
These 
indicators, 
combined 
with 
the 
more 
substantive 
analysis 
of 
the 
effectiveness 
of 
the 
PRS 
in 
the 
annual 
PHDRs 
and 
the 
annual 
PRS 
progress 
reports, 
will 
inform 
decisions 
on 
the 
continuation 
and 
design 
of 
subsequent 
PRSC support. 
A

with

7) 
are

Additionally,

of 
complementary 
mechanisms 
(see

13 
for

list) 
would 
allow for

fuller

of

in 
meeting 
the 
PRS

and

In

for

agriculture

development 
and 
PSD 
areas, 
are 
also 
being 
instituted.

78. 
The 
second 
level 
of 
results 
orientation 
refers 
to 
the 
impact 
of 
the 
actions 
identified 
in 
the 
PAF 
policy 
matrix. 
These 
actions 
are 
broadly 
intended 
to 
create 
an  adequate 
policy 
and 
institutional 
framework that 
is 
conducive 
to 
the 
achievement 
of 
the 
PRS targets.  Results 
are 
defined 
as 
substantive 
policy 
and 
institutional 
changes, 
and 
the 
actions 
outlined 
in 
the 
PAF 
policy 
matrix 
are 
steps 
toward 
the 
achievement 
of 
these  results. 
Clearly, 
however, 
as 
for all 
donor- 
27 
Page  38
government 
programs, 
determining 
a 
one-on-one  correspondence 
between the 
PRSC 
and 
the 
achievement 
of 
the 
PRS 
targets (and 
MDGs) 
is 
impossible. 
In 
fact, 
the 
level 
of 
attribution 
of 
PRSC 
actions 
to 
PRS 
targets, 
and 
particularly 
to 
the 
MDGs, 
is 
equally 
difficult for 
the 
productive 
(in 
this 
case, 
for 
PSD 
and agriculture) and 
the 
social 
sectors. 
For 
example, 
the target 
of 
increasing 
the 
share 
of 
income 
or 
consumption 
of 
the 
poorest 
20 
percent 
of 
the 
population 
(one 
of 
the 
MDGs) 
is 
influenced 
by 
more 
than 
just 
interventions 
to 
generate

although

put

enhanced

that 
will 
support 
more

of 
the 
ongoing or upcoming

81. 
Country

last

was

82. 
Public 
expenditure 
management: 
Since 
1997, 
PERs 
have been 
carried 
out 
annually 
basis 
in 
a 
participatory 
process 
that 
brings 
together 
central and 
sectoral government 
institutions,

and

academic 
and

institutes, 
the

and

as 
well 
as

array 
of

who 
contribute 
actively 
to 
the 
annual 
PERs. The 
PER 
process 
in 
Tanzania 
28 
Page  39
provides 
support 
to 
the 
formulation 
of 
both 
the 
budget 
and 
the 
MTEF 
and 
reviews 
expenditure 
performance and 
budget 
management. 
It 
has 
been 
particularly 
supportive 
of 
the 
setting 
of 
clear 
expenditure 
priorities 
for

health,

and

agricultural 
research 
and 
extension, 
the 
judiciary, 
and 
HIV/AIDS.

84. 
Procurement: 
A 
country 
procurement 
assessment 
report (CPAR) 
was  prepared 
during 
fiscal 
2003, 
and 
annex 
10 presents 
the 
main 
findings. 
In 
recent 
years, 
the 
Bank 
has 
continuously 
assisted 
the 
government 
in 
redesigning 
its 
procurement 
system, 
undertaking reforms 
and 
making 
assessments 
of 
progress achieved 
along 
the 
way. 
In 
2001, 
Tanzania 
passed 
a 
new 
procurement 
law, 
underpinning 
the 
reforms, and 
the 
Ministry 
of 
Finance 
has 
issued 
regulations 
to 
guide 
their 
implementation. 
The 
drafts 
for 
the 
new 
law 
and 
regulations 
were 
reviewed 
by 
Bank 
procurement 
specialists 
and 
passed 
as 
a basis 
for 
effective controls 
and 
integrity. 
85. 
Environmental 
aspects: 
Tanzania’s 
PRSCl 
is 
a Sectoral 
Adjustment 
Credit 
(SECAC), 
and 
it 
has 
been 
classified 
as 
category 
C, 
hence 
no 
formal 
environment impact 
assessment 
(EIA) 
is 
required. 
However, 
in 
an 
effort 
to 
mainstream 
the 
environmental 
sustainability 
dimension 
into 
the 
PRSC 
process, 
the 
Bank 
has 
undertaken 
an analysis 
with 
the 
objective 
of 
identifying 
linkages 
between 
key 
macroeconomic 
and 
structural 
reforms 
policies 
and 
the 
environment. 
This 
analysis 
will 
develop 
a 
set 
of 
measures 
at 
both 
the 
national 
and 
the 
local 
government levels that 
can 
be 
taken 
to 
reduce 
poverty 
and 
enhance 
environmental 
sustainability 
of 
policy 
reforms. 
The 
underlying 
premise 
of 
the 
analysis 
is 
that 
environment 
and 
poverty 
are 
linked 
in 
three 
major 
ways: 
(1) 
Poverty 
reduction 
programs 
should 
not 
damage 
the 
resource 
base 
and 
the 
environment 
on 
which 
poor 
people 
depend 
for 
their 
livelihoods; 
(2) 
improving 
environmental conditions 
can 
help 
to 
reduce 
poverty 
and 
promote 
sustainable 
pro-poor  growth;  and 
(3) 
it 
is 
necessary 
to 
identify 
any 
mitigating 
measures, 
as 
needed, 
as 
part 
of 
policy 
dialogue. 
In 
working 
with 
the 
government and other 
development 
partners, 
the 
analysis 
should therefore 
help 
identify 
strategic 
entry points 
for 
mainstreaming 
key 
issues 
of 
the 
poverty-environment 
nexus 
in 
Tanzania 
into 
the 
PRSC 
process 
and 
ongoing 
policy 
reforms 
in 
general. 
In 
this 
regard, 
the 
PRSC2 and 
PRSC3 
reform 
agenda 
has 
specified 
actions 
to 
be 
implemented 
by 
the 
government. 
86. 
Poverty 
and Social Impact 
Analysis: 
Social 
assessments 
have 
been 
an 
integral 
part 
of 
the 
preparation 
process 
of 
the 
PRS 
as 
well 
as 
of 
the 
various 
sector 
programs. 
Participatory 
poverty 
assessments 
(PPAs) 
are 
being 
carried out 
as 
part 
of 
the 
monitoring 
of 
the 
PRS 
implementation. 
In 
addition, 
local 
independent research 
institutes have 
carried 
out 
a 
variety 
of 
social 
assessments 
of 
specific 
reform 
initiatives. 
The 
most 
recent 
of 
these are 
an 
assessment 
of 
the 
public 
perception 
of 
progress 
in 
implementing 
anticorruption 
plans and a 
PPA. 
The 
analytic 
agenda 
under 
the 
poverty 
monitoring 
master 
plan 
includes 
poverty 
and social 
impact 
assessments 
of 
key 
reforms 
monitored 
under  the 
framework. 
This 
includes 
work 
supported 
by 
the 
Bank 
011 
the 
impact 
of 
rural 
development 
reforms 
on 
poverty 
in 
Tanzania. 
The 
planned 
PSIA 
will 
inform 
the 
design 
of 
these 
rural 
development 
reforms 
and 
establish 
the 
baseline 
for 
the 
future 
evaluation 
of 
the 
effectiveness 
and 
impact 
of 
these 
reforms.

Page  40
87. 
In 
addition 
to 
the economic and 
sector 
work 
required 
as 
a 
basis 
for 
a 
PRSC, 
a 
number 
of 
cross-cutting 
assessments 
of 
the country’s 
social, structural, 
and 
sector 
development 
policies 
have 
been 
carried out 
during 
the 
past 
few 
years 
(figure 
4).

V. 
MEDIUM-TERM 
PROGRAM FOR 
POLICY 
DIALOGUE 
AND 
PERFORMANCE 
ASSESSMENT 
UNDER 
THE 
PRSC 
88. 
The 
medium-term 
program 
supports 
the 
implementation 
of 
Tanzania’s 
PRS, 
as 
summarized 
in 
the 
PRSP 
of 
2000 
and 
subsequent 
updates 
undertaken 
with 
annual  progress 
reports. 
Policy 
dialogue and 
the 
performance 
assessment 
framework 
under the 
PRSC 
focus 
on 
cross-cutting 
and 
institutional 
actions 
under 
the 
PRS 
themes. 
After 
the 
approval 
of 
Tanzania’s 
PRSP 
in 
2000, 
the 
first 
and second 
PRS 
progress reports 
updated 
subthematic 
coverage, 
but 
the 
main 
objectives have 
been 
retained. 
The 
PRS 
goals, 
including 
the 
policies 
to 
reach 
them 
and 
the 
indicators 
to 
monitor 
them, 
are described 
in 
the 
PRSC 
policy 
matrix. 
89. 
The 
broad 
thrust 
of 
the 
PRSC three-year 
program 
builds 
on 
recent macroeconomic  and 
structural 
reforms 
undertaken 
by 
Tanzania 
and 
focuses 
on 
the 
following 
areas 
of 
the 
PRS 
objectives: 
(a) 
Reducing income poverty through 
strengthening 
private 
sector 
participation 
to 
support 
increased 
growth 
of 
the 
rural 
economy and 
SMEs, 
on 
which 
the 
majority 
of 
Tanzania’s 
poor 
depend 
for 
their 
livelihood; 
(b) 
strengthening 
human  capabilities 
and 
social 
well-being 
through 
improved 
monitoring 
and  evaluation 
of 
sector 
programs 
to 
ensure 
achievement 
of 
outcomes 
and impacts 
on 
the 
livelihoods 
of 
Tanzanians; 
(c) 
sustaining 
an 
environment conducive 
to 
development 
by 
actions 
to 
maintain 
macroeconomic 
stability 
and a 
tax 
regime 
friendly 
to 
growth 
and 
PSD, 
improve 
effectiveness 
of 
delivery 
of 
public 
services at 
all 
levels 
of 
government, 
adopt 
a performance-based 
system 
in 
public 
service, 
strengthen 
the 
public 
watchdog 
role,  and 
minimize 
resource  leakage 
and 
improved 
accountability; 
and 
(d) 
ensuring 
environmentally 
sustainable 
development 
through 
mainstreaming environmental 
concerns 
in 
the 
PRS process. 
90. 
More 
specifically,  the focus 
of 
actions supported 
in 
the 
context 
of 
the 
PRSC 
interventions 
relates 
to 
measures 
aimed 
at 
reducing 
income 
poverty through efforts 
to 
boost 
GDP 
growth 
in 
the 
medium 
term 
by 
promoting higher 
private 
investment, 
reducing 
the 
cost 
of 
doing 
business, 
and 
enhancing 
the 
efficiency 
of 
the Tanzanian 
economy. 
Thus, 
to 
disseminate 
broadly 
the 
impact 
of 
both 
reforms 
and resultant 
growth to 
the 
rural 
income 
poor,  support 
will 
be 
directed 
to, 
among 
other 
things, 
enhancement 
of 
the 
profitability 
of 
agriculture 
in 
general-and 
of 
export products 
of 
rural origin 
in 
particular-through 
better 
quality, 
higher 
productivity, 
reduced 
marketing 
costs, 
improved 
access 
to 
markets, 
and 
removal 
of 
the 
institutional 
constraints 
remaining 
on 
rural 
activities. 
9 
1. 
In 
addition 
to 
continued efforts 
targeted at 
improving 
the 
private 
investment 
climate 
and 
strengthening  the  performance 
of 
the 
rural 
economy, 
there 
is 
now 
a  need 
to 
bring 
the 
development 
budget 
of 
the 
GOT 
in 
line 
with 
the 
strategic 
public 
investment requirements 
to 
meet 
the 
PRS targets 
and 
support 
the 
growth 
of 
the 
private 
sector 
contribution 
to 
the 
economy 
and 
livelihoods. 
In 
this 
regard,  focus 
should 
now 
turn 
to 
aligning 
government 
policies 
and 
expenditure programs 
with 
the 
objectives 
of 
the 
PRS 
and enhancing 
the 
efficiency 
of 
public 
service 
delivery. 
Support 
is 
also 
provided 
for building 
on 
processes 
that 
have 
been 
put 
in 
place 
to 
enhance 
the 
strategic 
allocation 
of 
public 
resources 
for 
poverty 
reduction, 
increasing 
the 
* 
The 
PRSC 
policy 
matrix 
(or 
PAF) 
provides a substantially 
harmonized 
set 
of 
policy 
actions 
in 
support 
of 
the 
PRS. 
In 
the context 
of 
the 
PRSC, 
both 
the 
PRBS 
donors 
and 
the 
World 
Bank 
will 
avoid introducing 
new 
targets, 
indicators, 
or 
measures 
that 
are 
outside the 
PAF 
and the 
IMF 
macroeconomic 
annex. 
It 
is 
the 
intention 
of 
the parties 
to 
harmonize 
the 
PRS 
action 
plan 
and 
the 
PAF 
completely 
within 
three 
years. The 
PAF 
will 
be used 
as 
a 
tool 
for 
dialogue 
on 
PRS 
implementation 
and progress, 
and 
PAF 
actions 
will 
help to 
determine appropriate levels 
of 
future funding for 
the 
general 
budget. 
Through a continuous 
process, 
it 
will 
allow 
the government and 
the 
donors 
to 
assess 
progress 
toward 
agreed 
medium-term 
objectives 
and 
the 
implementation 
status 
of 
specific 
measures. 
32 
Page  43
efficiency 
of 
public 
resource 
use 
through 
measures 
to 
further 
strengthen 
accountability 
mechanisms 
combined 
with 
capacity 
building 
at 
the 
local 
and central 
government levels. 
92. 
Governance 
and 
accountability 
strengthening 
measures 
are 
primarily 
aimed 
at 
improvement 
of 
public 
service 
delivery 
through 
the 
implementation 
of 
the 
key 
components 
of 
the 
PSRP, 
the 
local 
government 
reform 
program, and 
the 
legal 
sector reforms, 
as 
well 
as 
fiscal 
and 
fiduciary 
measures 
(primarily 
implementation 
of 
the 
key 
recommendations 
from 
the 
PER, 
the 
CFAA, 
and 
the 
poverty 
expenditure 
tracking 
assessment), 
aimed 
at 
strengthening 
public 
expenditure 
management and enhancing transparency. 
93. 
Finally, 
a 
crucial 
ingredient 
in 
the 
effective  implementation 
of 
the 
PRS 
is 
a 
robust 
mechanism 
for 
regular and 
adequate 
monitoring 
of 
poverty, 
social 
well-being,  and 
environmental 
sustainability 
information 
and 
related 
analyses 
to 
facilitate 
a 
meaningful 
assessment 
of 
the 
PRS 
process. 
The 
program 
will 
support 
the 
Tanzania’s 
efforts 
to 
foster 
an effective 
monitoring 
and 
evaluation 
mechanism. 
94. 
Details 
of 
the program 
components 
are 
presented 
below 
under 
respective 
themes. 
Schedule 
2 
presents 
the 
PRSCl 
policy 
matrix, 
which 
contains 
a 
summary 
of 
actions and outcomes 
of 
the 
three-year program,  and annex 
7 
presents 
a 
preliminary 
list 
of 
key 
poverty 
outcome and 
impact 
monitoring 
indicators 
consistent 
with 
the 
MDGs. 
A. 
REDUCING 
INCOME 
POVERTY 
Private 
Sector Development 
(PSD) 
95. 
The 
Letter 
of 
Development 
Policy 
(LDP) 
for 
the 
ongoing 
Tanzania 
PSACl 
identified 
a 
set 
of 
actions 
in 
support 
of 
private 
sector 
growth 
to 
be 
implemented 
over 
a 
four-year 
period. 
It 
focused 
on 
improving 
the 
private 
investment 
climate through improved 
economic 
governance, 
improved 
business 
environment, 
privatization 
and 
regulation 
favoring 
competition. 
Actions 
for 
improving 
the 
business 
environment 
target 
legal 
reforms 
for 
enforcing property 
rights, 
further 
lowering 
the 
business 
costs 
of 
the 
tax 
regime,  and 
minimizing 
the 
scope 
for 
policy 
reversals. 
Privatization 
and  regulation 
target 
the 
provision 
of 
lower-cost 
and 
adequate 
infrastructure 
services 
to help 
reduce 
the 
cost 
of 
doing 
business 
in 
Tanzania and strengthen 
the 
competitiveness 
of 
Tanzanian 
business. 
PSACl 
supported 
the 
implementation 
of 
these 
actions 
for 
the 
first 
two 
years. 
Tangible 
results 
include 
the 
advancement 
of 
the 
privatization 
agenda, 
with 
government 
disengagement 
from 
commercial 
activities  almost  completed 
and 
significant 
progress 
toward 
greater 
private 
sector 
involvement 
in 
the 
provision 
of 
utilities; 
progress 
in 
strengthening 
the 
business 
environment 
by 
restructuring 
the 
Tanzania  Investment 
Center  and 
reform 
of 
land 
legislation; 
and 
the 
establishment 
of 
an 
improved regulatory 
environment. 
The 
proposed 
PRSC 
operation 
will 
pick 
up 
the 
key 
residual 
actions 
to 
ensure 
continuity 
of 
support 
for 
this 
agenda 
and, 
where 
applicable,  sharpen 
its 
poverty 
focus. 
The 
key 
areas 
reflected 
in 
the 
PRSC 
policy matrix 
are 
as 
follows: 
96. 
Inadequacies 
of 
the 
Land 
and Village 
Acts 
and 
slow 
implementation 
of 
their 
provisions: 
As 
agreed 
between 
the 
GOT 
and 
the 
private 
sector 
during 
the 
IRT 
of 
July 
2002, 
the 
Land 
Act, 
as 
currently 
drafted 
poses 
practical 
difficulties 
in 
relation 
to 
collateralization, 
foreclosure,  consent 
by 
spouse, 
customary 
and 
small 
mortgage, 
default 
notice,  and 
third-party 
mortgage. 
Slow 
implementation 
of 
the 
provision 
of 
the 
Land 
and 
Village 
Acts-in 
particular, 
the 
substantial 
delays 
in 
issuing 
title 
deeds, 
is 
also 
of 
concern. 
As 
part 
of 
the 
PRSCl 
actions  and 
after 
consultations 
with 
stakeholders, 
the 
Ministry 
of 
Lands 
has 
prepared 
a 
position 
paper 
outlining 
any 
33 
Page  44
changes 
that 
may 
be 
necessary 
to 
the 
Land 
Acts. 
As 
part 
of 
the 
trigger conditions 
for 
the 
PRSC2, 
after 
approval 
of 
the 
proposed 
changes 
to 
the 
Land 
Acts, the government 
will 
draft 
amendments 
to 
the 
Land 
Acts 
and 
submit 
them 
to 
parliament 
for 
approval. 
A 
tentative 
action 
for 
the 
PRSC3 
is 
the 
preparation 
and 
approval 
by 
government 
of 
the 
regulations 
for 
implementing 
the 
amended 
Land 
Acts. 
97. 
Lack 
of 
a 
coherent 
and 
comprehensive 
PSD 
strategy 
and 
SME 
policy: 
There 
is 
currently 
no 
comprehensive 
strategic 
framework 
to 
help 
with 
coordination 
and 
targeting 
of 
the various 
initiatives 
in 
support 
of 
PSD. 
The 
efforts 
so 
far, 
although 
commendable, 
appear 
to 
be 
piecemeal. 
Recognizing 
the 
importance 
of 
SMEs 
in 
employment 
creation 
and 
income 
generation 
and 
the 
need 
to 
encourage 
SME 
development, 
the 
Ministry 
of 
Industry 
and Trade 
has 
prepared 
an 
SME 
policy. 
The 
government 
has 
approved 
the 
policy 
for 
SME 
development 
as 
envisaged 
under 
the 
PRSCl 
policy 
matrix 
and launched 
a 
campaign 
for 
public 
awareness 
of 
the 
SME 
development 
policy. 
An 
indicative 
action 
for 
the 
PRSC2 
is 
to 
begin implementation 
of 
the 
policy 
in 
fiscal 
2004. 
The 
government 
has 
also begun 
the 
preparation 
of 
an 
integrated 
PSD 
strategy 
(involving 
comprehensive 
stakeholder  dialogue) 
under 
the  PRSC 1. 
Under 
indicative 
PRSC2 
actions,  the 
government 
will 
complete the preparation 
of 
and 
approve 
the 
PSD 
strategy document, 
which 
will 
include mainstreaming 
SME 
development. 
98. 
Rigid 
labor 
laws  impede 
market-oriented 
deployment 
of 
labor: 
Some 
administrative 
barriers 
to 
the 
importation 
of 
skilled 
labor 
still 
exist 
and 
inconsistencies  and 
contradictions 
remain 
between 
what 
the 
Tanzania Investment 
Center 
presents 
to 
investors 
and 
the 
requirements 
of 
the 
department 
of 
immigration. 
There 
is 
no 
single 
comprehensive 
labor 
law: 
It 
is 
currently 
encompassed 
in 
six 
different, 
outdated pieces 
of 
legislation. 
The 
Ministry 
of 
Labour 
is 
leading 
a 
process 
of 
consultations 
with 
stakeholders 
that 
is 
expected 
to 
lead 
to 
the 
definition 
of 
a 
new 
labor 
policy. 
This 
process 
is 
being 
fast-tracked under 
the 
follow-up 
action 
plan 
from 
the 
IRT 
held 
in 
July 
2002. 
Under 
indicative 
actions 
for 
the 
PRSC2, 
after 
consultations 
with 
stakeholders, 
the 
government 
will 
prepare 
a 
new 
labor 
policy 
and 
approve 
it. 
Subsequently, 
in 
the context 
of 
PRSC3 a 
new 
Labor

will 
be 
prepared and presented 
to 
parliament 
for 
approval. 
99. 
Need 
to 
improve 
the 
investment 
and 
business 
environment: 
Although 
the 
macroeconomic 
environment 
has 
been 
stabilized

improve 
the 
business 
climate, 
there 
remains 
a 
significant 
unfinished 
agenda 
in 
enhancing 
the 
investment climate. 
In 
July 
2002, 
the 
GOT 
approved 
the 
BEST 
program 
for 
carrying 
forward 
the 
reform 
agenda 
to 
improve 
the 
business

partly 
supported 
by 
the 
PSAC 
1. 
To 
complete 
one 
of 
the 
prior 
actions 
for 
the 
PRSCl, 
the 
steering 
committee 
of 
the  integrated 
framework 
for 
trade 
has 
approved 
the 
implementation 
plan 
for 
the 
BEST 
program. 
For 
the 
first 
phase 
of 
implementation (July 
2003- 
June 2004), 
the 
plan 
targets 
eight 
priority 
areas 
of 
action: (1) 
harmonization 
of 
local 
government 
taxation 
to 
remove 
excessive 
tax 
burden 
on 
private 
enterprise; 
(2) 
resolution 
of 
outstanding 
issues 
emanating 
from 
the 
Land 
Act; 
(3) 
review 
and 
amendment 
of 
labor 
laws constraining 
business 
operations; 
(4) 
streamlining 
of 
work 
permit 
procedures; 
(5) 
review 
and 
amendment 
of 
licensing 
legislation 
to 
reduce 
the 
cost 
of 
business 
establishment and 
continuation; 
(6) 
review 
and 
revision 
of 
export-import 
procedures 
to 
reduce 
time 
costs 
and 
corruption-related 
costs; 
(7) 
development 
of 
competition policy, 
mainly 
using 
advice 
given 
by 
the 
FIAS; 
and 
(8) 
design and 
implementation 
of 
a 
program 
for 
enhancing 
access 
to 
commercial 
courts 
by 
SMEs. 
The 
establishment 
of 
the 
Better 
Regulation 
Unit 
in

Office-Planning 
and

to

efficiency 
indicators 
from 
these 
actions, 
are 
essential 
for 
successful 
implementation 
and 
M&E 
of 
the 
program.

10 
1. 
Streamlining 
local 
government taxes 
and 
levies: 
The 
proliferation 
of 
local 
government 
taxes 
and levies 
has 
continued 
to 
be a serious 
issue, 
particularly 
because 
the 
complex 
local 
government 
revenue system 
has 
been 
characterized 
by 
very 
high 
compliance 
and 
administrative 
costs 
as 
well 
as 
considerable 
inefficiency. 
The 
PRSC 
policy matrix 
identifies 
measures 
aimed 
at 
simplifying 
and 
rationalizing local 
government 
taxation 
via 
the 
development 
of 
a strategy 
for 
such 
harmonization 
and 
issuance 
of 
related 
guidelines 
to 
local 
authorities. 
The 
measures 
aimed 
at 
addressing 
the 
key 
issues 
in 
this 
respect are discussed 
in 
some 
detail 
in 
the 
context 
of 
Section 
V.C 
on 
Sustaining 
Macroeconomic Stability. 
Rural 
Development 
102. 
The 
PRSC 
agenda 
with 
respect 
to 
addressing 
the 
challenges 
of 
rural 
development 
is 
focused 
on 
strategic 
planning;  capacity and 
institutional 
arrangement 
for 
implementation 
of 
the 
Agriculture 
Sector 
Development 
Strategy 
(ASDS); 
the 
regulatory 
and 
institutional environment 
for 
agricultural 
trade 
(specifically  taxation 
and 
the 
crop 
boards); 
the 
legal, 
regulatory,  and 
supervisory 
framework 
for 
microfinance; 
implementation 
of 
the 
Land 
Act 
and 
Village 
Land 
Act; 
and 
improvement 
of 
rural 
roads. 
103. 
Accelerated implementation 
of 
the 
ASDP: 
Through broad 
consultation, 
the 
GOT 
prepared 
an 
ASDS 
in 
2001 
and 
intends 
to 
operationalize 
the 
strategy 
through 
an 
ASDP. 
The 
ASDP 
framework 
and 
process document 
prepared 
by 
government 
(a 
PRSCl 
prior 
action) 
provide 
a 
sector-wide 
framework 
for 
overseeing 
the 
institutional, 
expenditure, and 
investment 
priorities 
in 
the 
agricultural 
sector 
and 
will 
be 
the 
government's 
main 
instrument 
for 
coordinating 
and 
monitoring 
agricultural 
development 
in 
the 
country. 
More 
specifically,  the 
ASDP 
will 
establish 
management 
and 
coordination 
procedures 
for 
ASDS 
implementation, 
identify 
priority 
interventions, 
facilitate 
detailed 
formulation 
and 
coordinated 
implementation 
of 
these 
interventions, 
establish  stakeholders' 
forums 
with 
adequate 
representation  and 
participation, 
enhance 
coordination 
of 
cross-sectoral 
issues, 
monitor 
progress, 
and 
assess 
impact. 
Priority 
areas 
of 
the 
ASDP 
include 
the 
policy, 
regulatory,  and 
institutional 
environment;  research 
and 
advisory 
services; 
PSD; 
marketing; 
rural 
finance, 
and 
cross 
cutting 
issues 
of 
land 
and 
rural 
roads. 
This 
should 
result 
in 
lower 
transactions cost 
of 
priority-focused 
interventions 
and 
improve agricultural 
productivity 
and 
profitability, 
the 
key 
objectives 
of 
the 
ASDS. 
104. 
The 
division 
of 
the 
main 
agriculture 
ministry 
into 
three 
separate 
ministries 
(ministries 
of 
agriculture and 
food 
security,  cooperatives and 
marketing; 
and 
livestock 
and 
water) 
is 
creating 
particular 
challenges 
for 
implementation. 
Efficiency 
of 
resources 
used 
and  effectiveness 
of 
service 
delivery 
remain 
key 
concerns. 
The 
fixed 
costs 
associated 
with 
the 
creation 
of 
multiple 
structures 
is 
high, 
and 
problems 
of 
coordination 
and 
duplication 
of 
activities 
have 
hampered 
development 
of 
the ASDP, 
with 
concerns 
that 
these 
will 
persist 
through 
implementation. 
As 
a 
prior 
action 
for 
the 
PRSCl 
the 
government 
has 
finalized 
the 
ASDP 
framework 
and 
process 
document and 
adopted 
it 
for 
implementation.

106. 
Further 
review 
and clarification 
of 
the 
roles 
and funding  arrangements 
of 
crop boards: 
The regulatory 
and 
institutional 
environment 
continues 
to 
constrain 
incentives 
for 
agricultural 
export 
growth, 
including 
the 
functioning 
of 
crop 
boards and 
local 
government taxation. 
The 
marketing 
liberalization 
begun 
in 
the 
mid-1990s 
increased 
the 
farmers’ 
share 
of 
the 
border 
price 
37 
Page  48
and 
induced 
higher 
levels 
of 
private 
sector 
investment 
in 
new 
processing 
facilities 
(e.g., 
for 
cashews). 
However, 
in 
many 
cases, 
these 
more 
favorable 
policies 
have 
not 
been 
sustained. 
Export 
crops  are 
currently 
heavily 
taxed, 
heavily 
regulated, 
and  vulnerable 
to 
frequent 
political 
interventions 
that have 
acted 
to 
constrain producer incentives. 
Unnecessary 
regulation 
has 
led 
to 
delays 
in 
marketing,  reduced 
private 
sector 
confidence 
in 
investing 
in 
the 
sector, 
and 
lowered 
prices 
to 
producers. 
Crop 
boards  have  a  substantial 
influence 
on 
agricultural  export  crop 
development 
in 
Tanzania 
and 
their 
roles and 
funding 
arrangements 
need 
to 
be 
further 
reviewed 
and 
clarified 
in 
the 
context 
of 
the 
ongoing 
concerns 
of 
local 
government 
taxation 
and 
actions 
by 
the 
boards 
that 
have 
not 
always 
been 
in 
the 
best 
interest 
of 
crop producers. 
Delineation 
of 
the 
regulatory, 
service, 
and 
tax 
functions 
by 
public 
and 
private 
sector 
activities 
will 
be 
necessary. 
Key 
areas 
for 
review 
are 
(a) 
clarifying 
and 
limiting 
to 
regulatory functions 
the 
role 
of 
the 
boards, 
(b) 
options 
for 
funding 
the 
crop 
boards 
through 
the 
budget 
and 
removing 
their 
taxation 
function, 
(c) 
removing 
their 
service 
functions 
for 
provision 
by 
the 
private 
sector, 
and 
(d) 
the 
structures 
to 
undertake the 
regulatory functions 
(options 
to 
be 
explored include 
the 
crop 
boards 
as 
separate 
entities 
or 
a 
single 
regulatory 
body). 
Actions 
to 
address 
these issues are 
included 
in 
the 
PAF 
under 
the 
PRSC2 
and 
PRSC3. 
Indicative 
actions 
under 
the 
PRSC2 
include 
agreement 
on 
the 
scope 
and 
modalities 
of 
the review, 
completion 
of 
the 
review 
for 
broader stakeholder discussion, 
and subsequently 
(tentative 
PRSC3 action) amendment 
of 
the 
Crop 
Board 
Acts 
based 
on 
findings 
and 
proposals 
of 
the 
review. 
In 
the 
meantime, 
the  government 
will 
consider 
administrative 
measures 
that 
could 
be 
taken 
to 
address 
these 
concerns. 
107. 
Strengthen 
the 
legal, 
regulatory, 
and 
supervisory 
framework 
for 
microfinance: 
Removing 
constraints 
to 
the 
overall 
business 
environment 
should 
raise 
returns 
to 
economic 
activity 
and 
demand 
for 
financial 
services. 
The 
government 
should 
avoid 
supporting 
any 
distortionary  interventions 
on 
the 
supply 
side, 
such 
as 
the 
establishment 
of 
new  financial 
institutions, 
because these are 
no 
more 
likely 
to 
overcome 
the 
existing 
hurdles 
than 
the 
current 
financial 
institutions. 
Past 
interventions 
have 
not 
worked. 
There have 
been 
a 
number 
of 
efforts 
to 
ensure 
the 
emergence 
of 
more 
efficient 
and  sustainable 
financial 
intermediaries. 
A 
national 
microfinance  policy, 
designed 
along 
industry 
best practices,  was 
prepared 
through 
extensive 
consultation 
with 
microfinance 
donors, 
practitioners, 
and 
other stakeholders. 
It 
was 
approved 
by 
the 
GOT 
and 
in 
place 
by 
May 
2000. 
The 
first 
National 
Conference 
on 
Microfinance, 
whose 
aim 
was 
to 
disseminate 
the 
policy 
and 
provide 
a 
forum 
for 
stakeholders 
to 
formulate 
respective 
implementation 
strategies, 
was 
held 
in 
March 
2001. 
As 
part 
of 
the 
PRSCl 
program, 
the 
government prepared recommendations 
for 
the 
legal, 
regulatory, 
and 
supervisory 
framework 
for 
microfinance, 
consistent 
with 
the 
national microfinance 
policy 
and, 
based 
on 
recommendations, 
prepared 
corresponding 
legislation that 
has 
been 
passed 
by 
parliament. 
Enforcement 
of 
this 
legislation 
is 
an 
indicative 
PRSC2 action. 
108. 
Improve 
land tenure 
security: 
Enactment 
of 
the 
Land 
Act 
and 
Village 
Land 
Act 
in 
1999 
was 
a 
positive 
step 
toward 
solving land 
tenure 
issues 
in 
Tanzania. 
The 
acts 
create 
avenues 
to 
resolve 
problems 
related 
to 
tenure 
insecurity, 
particularly 
for 
women, 
by 
providing 
a 
legal 
basis 
for 
regularizing land 
tenure 
under 
customary 
tenure 
regimes 
and 
providing for 
decentralized 
land 
administration 
and 
conflict 
resolution. 
This 
will 
be 
particularly important 
in 
areas 
with 
rising 
population 
pressure 
and 
agricultural 
commercialization. 
The 
centerpiece 
of 
the 
laws 
is 
the 
devolution 
of 
authority 
and 
administration 
over 
land 
to 
the 
village 
councils. 
The 
councils 
are 
now 
responsible 
for 
guiding 
community 
decisions 
on 
the 
distribution 
of 
land 
within 
the 
village 
into 
household, clan, 
community, 
and other 
lands, 
as 
well 
as 
their 
adjudication, 
registration (village 
land 
register), 
and 
titling 
(to 
be 
effected 
by 
the 
office 
of 
the 
commissioner 
for 
lands 
in 
accordance 
with 
the 
decisions 
of 
the village). 
Since 
the 
enactment 
of 
the 
Land 
Act 
in 
1999, 
implementation 
has 
been 
slow. 
Under 
the 
PRSC program, focus 
is 
given 
to 
accelerating 
implementation 
progress 
. 
As 
such, 
the 
policy 
actions 
under 
the 
PRSC 
policy  matrix 
include 
the 
development 
of 
a 
38 
Page  49
prioritized 
strategic 
plan 
for 
implementation 
of 
the 
acts. 
However, 
full 
(country-wide) 
implementation 
of 
the 
acts 
in 
the 
next 
few 
years 
will 
likely 
be 
unaffordable 
and 
constrained 
by 
limited 
capacity. 
The 
strategic 
plan 
should 
prioritize 
initial 
implementation 
to 
areas 
where 
the 
impact 
is 
likely to 
be 
greatest. 
Based 
on 
the 
plan, 
a 
program 
to 
strengthen 
capacity 
for 
implementation, 
at 
both 
the 
national 
and 
local 
levels, 
should 
be developed. 
Both 
of 
these 
items 
are 
included 
under 
indicative 
PRSC2 actions. 
The 
implementation 
of 
the 
prioritized 
plan 
is 
to 
begin over 
the 
medium 
term 
(tentative PRSC3 action). 
1 
09. 
Strengthen 
the 
institutional 
arrangements 
for 
district 
road 
maintenance 
and 
rehabilitation: 
Improved 
market 
access 
is 
essential 
for 
the 
transformation 
of 
subsistence 
agriculture 
into 
commercial 
agriculture. Distance 
to 
markets remains 
large, 
and transaction 
costs 
are 
a 
large 
share 
of 
the 
cost 
of 
agricultural 
marketing. 
For 
example, a 
1999 
commodity marketing 
study 
concluded that 
approximately 
40 
percent 
of 
the cost 
of 
grains 
in 
the 
major 
urban 
markets 
is 
attributed 
to 
transportation 
costs. 
Only 
8 
percent 
of 
the 
districts’ 
road 
network 
are 
in 
good 
condition. 
Sixty 
percent 
of 
the 
district 
and 
feeder 
road network 
are 
impassable 
to 
vehicles 
throughout the 
year, 
increasing 
to 
90 
percent 
during 
the 
rainy 
season. 
Improved 
rural 
roads 
would 
raise 
the 
producer’s 
share 
of 
the 
export 
crop 
price,  reduce 
the 
farm-level 
cost 
of 
inputs, 
and 
reduce 
spatial 
marketing 
margins 
in 
food 
marketing. Implementation 
arrangement 
for 
maintaining 
and 
developing 
rural 
roads remains weak. 
In 
most districts, 
the 
capacity 
to 
plan,  organize, 
and 
manage 
road 
maintenance 
work 
is 
lacking, 
and 
coordination 
among 
the 
national, 
regional, 
and 
district 
engineers 
is 
weak. 
Improving 
the 
network 
of 
district 
and 
feeder roads 
would 
require 
a 
substantial 
increase 
in 
recurrent 
and 
investment 
expenditure,  and 
the 
use 
and  accounting 
of 
existing 
funds 
need 
to 
be 
improved, 
as 
highlighted 
in 
the 
recent  annual 
audit 
of 
road 
funds 
resources 
going to local 
levels. 
The 
PRSC 
policy matrix 
calls 
for 
institutional 
strengthening 
by 
development 
of 
proposals 
to 
strengthen 
the 
institutional 
arrangements 
for 
district  road 
maintenance and 
rehabilitation 
(an 
indicative 
PRSC2 
action), 
followed 
the 
next 
year 
(tentative 
PRSC3 
action) 
by 
beginning 
implementation 
of 
a 
program 
to 
strengthen 
institutional 
arrangements 
for 
district 
road 
maintenance and 
rehabilitation. 
B. 
MONITORING 
THE IMPLEMENTATION 
OF 
THE 
PRS 
110. 
An 
important 
feature 
of 
the 
Tanzania 
PRS 
is 
that 
it 
constitutes  a 
rolling, 
three-year 
framework 
for 
implementation 
of 
policies 
and 
measures 
to 
alleviate 
poverty 
in 
a 
manner that 
is 
both 
participatory 
and outcome 
oriented. 
This 
practical 
approach 
to 
ensuring 
that 
the 
PRS 
is 
a 
living 
document 
enables 
the 
PRS 
goals 
and 
implementation 
arrangements 
to 
be 
calibrated 
flexibly 
in 
the 
light 
of 
experience. 
It 
is 
therefore 
vital 
that 
implementation 
of 
the 
PRS 
is 
monitored 
adequately, 
and 
the 
results  should 
be 
evaluated 
effectively 
for 
further 
strengthening 
of 
the 
process. 
11 
1. 
The 
medium-term 
outcome 
being 
sought 
is 
enhanced 
accountability 
for 
delivery 
on 
the 
PRS 
via 
coordinated and 
streamlined 
monitoring 
processes 
across 
the 
GOT. 
An 
integral 
element 
of 
PRSC support 
thus 
will 
be 
linked 
to 
enhanced 
monitoring 
of 
progress 
toward 
the 
attainment 
of 
the 
PRS objectives. 
M&E 
in 
the 
context 
of 
the 
PRSC 
builds 
on 
a 
number 
of 
processes 
that 
are 
already 
in 
place 
or 
being 
developed 
to 
monitor 
and evaluate progress 
in 
the 
implementation 
of 
the 
PRS. 
Briefly, 
the 
current 
status 
of 
the 
system 
for 
poverty monitoring 
and 
analysis 
in 
Tanzania 
is 
as 
follows: 
0 
0 
A 
sound 
policy 
framework 
for 
poverty reduction 
is 
in 
place. 
The 
PRS process 
is 
demonstrating that 
it 
is 
an 
effective 
way to 
identify 
priority 
actions 
to 
reduce 
poverty. 
The 
GOT 
has 
prepared 
the 
second PRS 
progress 
report. 
39 
Page  50
0 
Tanzania 
is 
now 
in 
the 
process 
of 
integrating 
the 
MDGs 
and 
monitoring 
their 
progress 
in 
the 
PRS 
process. Tanzania 
produced 
a 
first 
report 
on 
progress 
toward 
the 
MDGs 
in 
2001 
and 
a 
report 
on 
costing 
the 
achievements 
of 
the 
MDGs 
in 
2002. 
This report 
also 
indicated 
the 
likelihood 
of 
achieving 
the 
targets 
for 
Tanzania. 
A 
report 
on 
progress 
toward 
achievement 
of 
the 
MDGs 
in 
Zanzibar 
is 
currently 
under 
way. 
A 
poverty 
monitoring 
master 
plan 
has 
been 
agreed 
to 
by 
stakeholders 
and 
published 
and 
distributed 
in 
Kiswahili 
and 
English 
versions. 
The 
master 
plan 
provides 
a 
comprehensive 
system 
for 
monitoring 
the 
various 
dimensions 
of 
poverty reduction 
and 
economic 
growth, 
as 
well 
as 
the 
implementation 
of 
the 
various 
elements 
of 
the 
PRS. 
The 
institutional 
arrangements 
for 
a 
poverty 
monitoring 
system 
have 
been agreed 
upon, 
comprising 
four 
technical 
working 
groups 
and 
a 
national 
committee. 
The 
technical 
working 
groups 
are 
concerned 
with 
surveys 
and 
censuses, 
routine 
data 
systems, 
research 
and 
analysis, 
and 
dissemination, sensitization, 
and 
advocacy. The 
institutional 
framework 
for 
poverty 
monitoring 
and 
evaluation 
is 
under the 
oversight 
of 
the 
Vice 
President’s 
Office 
and 
also 
overseen 
technically by 
a 
National 
Poverty 
Monitoring 
Steering Committee. 
There 
was 
an 
impressive 
set 
of 
key 
outputs 
of 
the 
poverty 
monitoring 
system 
during 
2002. 
These are 
the 
HBS, 
PHDR, 
National 
Participatory Poverty 
Assessment, and 
the 
conduct 
of 
the 
poverty 
policy 
week. 
The 
timing 
of 
PRS 
reviews 
has 
been 
adjusted 
for 
optimal 
link 
to 
budgeting 
and 
consultative 
group 
processes. 
Discussions 
on 
the 
links 
with 
the 
public 
expenditure 
review 
process have begun.

112. 
Hence, 
the

builds 
on

and

mechanism. 
These

to

Figure 
5 
provides an overview 
of 
the 
monitoring 
system, 
which 
covers outcome, output, 
process, 
and 
input 
indicators. 
This 
system 
comprises 
three 
interrelated 
tiers. 
The 
poverty 
monitoring 
system 
focuses 
on 
the 
measurement 
of 
impact, 
outcomes, 
and 
proxy 
indicators. 
Sector 
programs, such 
as 
those 
for 
education 
and health, focus 
on 
the 
tracking 
of 
output indicators 
with 
adequate 
monitoring 
mechanisms 
in 
place. 
The 
PER-MTEF 
processes 
focus 
on 
inputs, 
with 
an 
emphasis 
on 
budget 
allocation 
and 
budget execution. 
114. 
In 
the context 
of 
the 
PRSC 
and 
the 
PRS, 
outcome,  output, 
and 
input 
indicators 
provide 
direct 
information 
on 
the 
status 
of 
poverty 
in 
all 
its 
dimensions. 
Monitoring 
of 
these 
indicators 
is 
based 
on 
a 
broad 
range 
of 
surveys 
and administrative 
data 
systems 
identified 
in 
the 
poverty 
reduction 
master 
plan. 
The 
PHDR 
is 
expected 
to 
be 
produced 
annually, 
consolidate 
poverty 
measures 
from 
various 
sources, 
and 
provide 
analysis 
of 
poverty 
trends 
and 
underlying 
factors. 
(Annex 
12 
shows 
the 
agreed 
outline 
of 
the 
PHDR.) 
As 
noted, 
preliminary 
work 
on PSIA 
has 
been 
carried 
out 
to 
underpin 
the 
PHDR. Additionally, 
in 
fiscal 
2004, 
the 
GOT 
will 
undertake a 
poverty 
and 
social 
impact 
assessment 
and 
a 
poverty vulnerability 
study 
to 
strengthen 
analyses 
carried out 
41 
Page  52
so 
far 
and 
establish  a  stronger  baseline 
for 
future 
monitoring. 
A 
poverty

week

by

of

(VPO) 
in

The

is 
planned 
to

an

and

will 
focus

in

and

in

will

will

for

of

Progress 
in 
public

management 
covering 
both

in

and

and operational 
efficiency 
in

of

will 
be 
tracked 
by 
the 
annual 
PERs.

5. 
An

of

groupg 
for 
the

of 
the 
TAS. 
Additionally,

meetings 
provide

of

as

of 
the 
way 
forward 
as

related 
action 
plan 
by 
the 
donor 
community 
(locally

and

In

Group 
also

C. 
SUSTAINING 
MACROECONOMIC 
STABILITY 
130. 
Since 
the 
mid-l990s, 
Tanzania 
has 
made 
substantial 
progress 
in 
macroeconomic 
stabilization, 
structural 
and 
social 
reforms,  and 
the 
removal 
of 
key 
distortions 
in 
the 
economy. 
The 
macroeconomic  performance  remained  strong 
under 
the 
PRGF- 
and 
PSAC 
1 
-supported 
structural reforms 
programs. 
Recognizing 
that sustaining macroeconomic 
stability 
is 
imperative 
for 
higher 
growth 
and 
poverty 
reduction, 
the 
PRSC 
policy matrix 
places considerable emphasis 
on 
the 
second 
generation 
of 
reforms. 
In 
particular,  attention 
is 
devoted 
to 
two main 
areas 
of 
concern, 
which 
are 
discussed 
below. 
The 
PRBS 
framework includes 
10 
key bilateral 
donors 
and 
the 
European Commission. 
45 
Page  56
Maintaining 
Prudent  Fiscal 
and 
Monetary 
Policies 
and 
Ensuring  Prudential  Debt 
Contracting 
and 
ManagementI2 
13 
1. 
Tanzania’s 
public 
and 
publicly 
guaranteed 
external 
debt 
is 
assessed 
as 
being 
currently 
sustainable 
after 
obtaining 
irrevocable 
debt 
relief 
under 
the 
enhanced 
HIPC 
Initiative 
(amounting 
to 
US$ 
3 
billion). 
Continued sustainability 
of 
Tanzania’s 
external 
debt 
is 
contingent 
on 
the 
sustained

138. 
In

Tanzania 
has 
launched 
a 
number

to

(a)

(f)

(GGCU) 
in

and 
(g)

of

This 
ambitious 
reform 
agenda 
seeks 
to 
attack 
the

of

poor

Overall, 
sound  progress 
is

in

program. 
139. 
Among

plays

because

The

The

aims 
at 
transforming

into 
a service 
that 
has 
the

and

for 
client

and continuous 
improvement 
of 
services. 
Under 
the 
transformed 
public 
service, 
public 
servants 
will 
be 
held 
accountable 
for 
specified  outputs 
and  outcomes. 
Therefore,

PSRP 
seeks 
to 
introduce-in 
a 
phased, 
systematic

management 
environment 
based 
on 
performance and 
transparency. 
This 
is 
a 
long-term 
process 
intended 
to 
transform 
the 
public 
service 
into 
results-oriented 
management, 
which 
the 
Bank, 
along 
with 
other 
development 
partners, 
is 
supporting 
via 
a 
long-term 
APL. 
Strategic 
use 
of 
limited 
public

toward 
service 
improvements 
in 
line 
with

priorities 
and 
expenditures 
would

140. 
Pay 
reform 
was a 
prominent 
component 
of

Program. 
Beginning 
in 
fiscal 
1992/93,

a 
reversal 
of

Since

Furthermore,

This

effectively. 
In

The

restores

to

when

and

of

It 
is

annual 
pay 
awards 
in 
line 
with 
medium-term 
targets. 
Pay 
is 
also 
related 
to 
responsibilities 
through 
the 
implementation 
of 
the 
findings 
of

ongoing

MINIMIZING 
RESOURCE 
LEAKAGE 
AND

Fiduciary 
Accountability and Procurement 
143. 
With 
the

of

and 
the

Number 
6 
of 
200 
1 
and

Number 
3 
of 
200 
1, 
the 
PRSC 
program 
will 
help 
Tanzania make 
further

on 
the 
steps 
it 
has 
already 
taken 
to 
put 
into 
place 
a sound 
financial 
management

The

and

of

In

issues 
of 
noncompliance,

budget

capacity, 
and

of

need 
to

resolved. 
The 
specific

derives 
from 
the 
following 
key 
areas: 
(a) 
Central 
and 
local 
government accounting  and 
financial 
reporting 
are constrained

a shortage 
of 
qualified 
and

and

personnel 
because 
of 
the 
unattractive  terms  and

of 
employment. 
(b) 
There 
is 
a 
lack 
of 
effective 
measures 
to 
ensure

with 
fiduciary 
procedures, 
and 
there 
are 
weaknesses 
in 
government 
information

policy 
and

(c) 
Public 
sector 
auditing 
is 
inadequately 
resourced 
in 
terms 
of 
both

and

capacity. Furthermore, 
disparities 
prevail 
between 
audit and

staff 
with

the 
terms  and

of

The

Number 
6 
of 
2001 
bolsters the

to 
it. 
It

to

of

The

F. 
MAINSTREAMING 
THE 
ENVIRONMENT 
INTO 
THE 
PRSC 
PROCESS1s 
Background 
153. 
Tanzania 
is 
highly 
dependent 
on 
the 
use 
of 
natural 
resources 
and 
biodiversity 
for 
its 
economic 
growth 
and development, 
because 
agriculture, 
tourism 
(almost 
all 
of 
it 
nature-based), 
and 
mining 
being 
the 
mainstays 
of 
the 
economy. 
Poverty 
is 
widespread, 
especially 
in 
rural 
areas 
where almost 
all 
of 
the 
income 
is 
based 
on 
natural 
resources. 
A 
key 
source 
of 
vulnerability 
of 
the 
poor 
is 
the degradation 
and 
depletion 
of 
the 
environmental 
and 
natural 
resource 
base. 
Several 
steps 
have 
been taken 
to 
create a sound basis 
for 
addressing 
environmental 
degradation.  These 
include 
the 
national environmental action 
plan 
(1994) 
and 
the 
national environmental 
policy 
l4 
The 
judiciary; 
the 
ministries 
of 
works, 
education 
and 
culture, 
health, 
and 
home 
affairs; 
the 
attorney 
general’s 
chambers; 
and 
the 
TRA. 
l5 
It 
is 
noteworthy that 
the 
measures 
included 
in 
the 
PRSC 
policy 
matrix 
with 
respect 
to 
mainstreaming 
of 
the 
environment 
are 
exclusive to 
the 
PRSC 
instrument 
and 
are 
not 
supported 
in 
the 
context 
of 
the 
PRBS 
facility. 
51 
Page  62
(1 
997). 
An 
institutional 
and 
legal 
framework 
for 
environmental 
management, 
providing 
the 
basis 
for 
environmental  impact 
assessment 
(EIA), 
cross-sectoral 
coordination, 
and 
integration 
of 
environmental 
management 
into 
local 
government 
planning 
processes, 
was 
approved 
by 
the 
cabinet 
in 
December 
2002. 
A 
number 
of 
key 
sector 
policies 
and 
strategies 
recognize 
the 
need 
to 
address 
poverty reduction 
objectives 
through 
mainstreaming 
environmental 
sustainability. 
These 
strategies 
include 
tourism, 
women 
and 
gender, 
rural 
development, 
agriculture,  forestry,  and 
fisheries 
and 
coastal 
management. 
Framework for  Mainstreaming 
the Environment into the 
PRSC 
Process 
154. 
The 
importance 
of 
environmental 
sustainability 
on 
poverty 
reduction efforts 
is 
expressed 
via 
the 
MDGs. 
The 
cross-sectoral nature 
of 
the environment and 
its 
direct 
and 
indirect 
linkages 
to 
the 
MDGs 
provide 
an 
opportunity 
to 
address 
its 
critical role 
in 
Tanzania’s 
economic 
growth 
and 
poverty reduction 
agenda 
through 
the 
PRSC process. 
Mainstreaming 
of 
the 
environment 
in 
the 
poverty  reduction 
agenda 
is 
a 
specific  target 
within 
the 
MDGs, 
expressed 
through 
Goal 
7: 
Ensuring  Environmental  Sustainability. 
Effective 
integration 
of 
the 
environment 
into 
policy 
reforms 
requires 
building 
strong 
partnerships 
through 
extensive 
consultation 
and  partnership 
processes. 
Mainstreaming 
of 
the 
environment 
into 
the PRSC process 
will 
be carried out 
by 
the 
VPO 
with 
the support 
of 
the 
United 
Nations Development 
Programme (UNDP), 
the 
Bank, the 
donor community, 
and  other 
stakeholder  groups. 
It 
is 
envisaged 
that 
the 
PRSC  process 
will 
operationalize 
high-priority 
activities 
already 
identified 
by 
the 
GOT 
for 
mainstreaming 
the 
environment 
into 
the 
PRS. 
The 
implementation 
of 
the 
policy 
approach 
for 
mainstreaming 
environment 
into 
the 
PRS 
and 
to 
promote 
pro-poor 
growth 
is 
reflected 
in 
a 
number 
of 
interventions financed 
by 
World 
Bank 
and 
bilateral 
donors. 
Examples 
of 
this 
new 
generation 
of 
initiatives 
include 
programs 
in 
forestry, 
agriculture, 
and coastal 
livelihoods. 
Specific 
actions 
supported 
by 
the 
PRSC 
include: 
155. 
Increasing 
the 
knowledge 
base 
on 
poverty-environment linkages: 
Lack 
of 
knowledge 
and 
awareness 
about 
environment 
and 
poverty 
linkages 
could 
lead 
to 
missed 
opportunities 
and 
efficiency 
in 
the 
government’s 
poverty reduction 
efforts, and 
this 
could 
increase 
the 
vulnerability 
of 
the 
poor 
to 
environmental 
risks. 
Mainstreaming 
of 
the 
environment 
into 
the 
PRS 
agenda 
is 
a 
dynamic 
process 
that 
will 
become 
more 
effective 
as 
more knowledge 
and 
awareness 
about 
the 
linkages among 
the 
environment,  poverty,  and economic 
growth 
become 
available. 
The 
PRSC 
will 
generate 
this 
knowledge  through 
supporting 
analytical 
work 
on 
poverty-environment 
linkages, 
which 
will 
be 
used 
to 
provide 
inputs 
into 
the 
PRS-PER 
process, 
and  sectoral  and 
district-level

Establishing 
an 
effective, 
integrated 
environmental 
assessment 
process: 
Lack 
of 
sufficient  institutional 
capacity 
for 
integrated 
environmental 
assessment, 
including 
EIA 
and 
strategic 
environmental 
assessment 
(SEA), 
could 
limit 
the 
achievement 
of 
sustainable 
growth 
and 
development, 
it 
and 
may 
delay 
the 
implementation 
of 
certain 
PRSC 
actions-and 
through 
this, 
effective implementation 
of

Tanzania’s 
PRSC 
process intends 
to 
go 
beyond 
the 
Bank’s 
requirements 
for 
EIA 
and 
seeks 
to 
mainstream 
EIA 
and 
SEA 
as 
a 
planning 
and management 
tool 
to 
provide 
inputs 
and 
feedback 
to 
enhance 
sustainability 
of 
sectoral 
reform 
programs 
and 
provide 
inputs 
to 
sectoral 
and 
district 
plans. 
However, 
before 
the 
EIA 
and 
SEA 
can 
be 
effectively 
integrated 
into 
sectoral 
and 
district  planning 
processes,

is 
a

to

related

it.

recently

for

management 
is 
effectively 
implemented 
to 
strengthen 
the

in

country. 
This 
is 
of

to 
ensure 
(a) 
that 
the 
environmental 
assessment 
process 
provides 
a basis 
for 
sound

(b) 
transparency 
in 
regulatory 
mechanisms and effectiveness 
in 
institutional 
coordination,  and 
(c) 
improved 
public 
consultation 
process. 
The 
PRSC 
will 
support 
the 
development 
of 
environmental 
assessment 
(ETA 
and 
SEA) 
processes and 
guidelines 
with

to

poverty 
and 
livelihoods

and

into 
sectoral and 
local 
government 
policy 
and 
planning 
processes. 
Finally, 
the 
PRSC 
process 
will 
support 
capacity 
building 
within 
the 
division 
of 
environment, 
the 
poverty

for

(b)

sectoral, 
and 
district 
levels; 
and

strengthening 
partnerships 
for 
environmental 
and 
poverty 
monitoring.

Aspects 
173. 
Aside 
from

supported

in 
place that 
aim 
at 
improved

and transparency 
for

of

The  Prevention 
of 
Corruption 
Bureau 
and 
the 
National 
Audit 
Office 
have 
been 
significantly 
strengthened 
during 
recent 
years, 
and 
the 
Bank 
is 
preparing a 
project that 
would 
support 
further 
strengthening 
of 
accountability 
mechanisms. The 
participatory 
PER-MTEF 
process 
provides 
for 
an 
open 
review 
of 
budgetary  performance. 
The 
CFAA 
on 
Tanzania  concluded 
that 
the  central  and 
local 
government 
financial 
management 
systems 
represent 
high fiduciary 
risk. 
The 
major 
recommendations contained 
in 
that  report 
have 
been 
reflected 
in 
the 
reform 
program 
supported 
by 
the 
PRSC. 
To 
ensure 
effective  implementation 
of 
the  reform,  the  government 
has 
developed 
the 
PFMRP,  the 
implementation 
of 
which 
will 
be
